`isComputableSplit_ofBisection` takes them instead. **New work beyond the plan**: `IsComputableSplit`'s `posIdx_primrec`/`negIdx_primrec` fields demand the *joint* primitive-recursiveness of the index function as a single `Nat.Primrec` witness of the packed triple `t.unpair.1, t.unpair.2.unpair.1, t.unpair.2.unpair.2` (`IsComputableSplit`'s own coding convention) ‚Äî `posIdxFromBisection`/`negIdxFromBisection` were previously only known primitive recursive *compositionally* (built from primitive-recursive pieces) but never packaged this way, so `primrec_posIdxFromBisection`/`primrec_negIdxFromBisection` needed proving fresh (mirroring `LevelSetPrimrec.lean`'s `primrec_myUpsample` triple-argument idiom): unpack `t`'s three projections, feed `Nat.pair n k` through `primrec_emptyInterDec`/`primrec_emptyDiffDec`, chain two `primrec_selectFn` applications, and close with `.of_eq fun _ => rfl` (the packed and curried forms are definitionally equal, no `unpair_pair` massaging needed since no `Nat.pair`/`unpair` round-trip occurs). `splitFromBisection A B' Xn` is a `dite` on `‚àÉ n m k, A = P.X n ‚àß B' = Q.X m ‚àß Xn = P.X k` (order chosen to match `posIdxFromBisection`'s own `(n, m, k)` argument order, simplifying the nested `Exists.choose`/`choose_spec` extraction versus the plan's `(n, k, m)` ordering), landing on `(Q.X (posIdxFromBisection ‚Ä¶ h.choose h.choose_spec.choose h.choose_spec.choose_spec.choose), ‚Ä¶)` when it holds, `(B', B')` (never read downstream) otherwise. `isComputableSplit_ofBisection` needed a `noncomputable def` (not `theorem`) ‚Äî `IsComputableSplit` is a data-carrying `structure` (its `posIdx`/`negIdx` fields are `‚Ñï`-valued functions), not a `Prop`, so `theorem ... where` fails elaboration ("is not a proposition"); `posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec` then proceed exactly per plan: `unfold`, `dif_pos` at the trivial witness `‚ü®n, m, k, rfl, rfl, rfl‚ü©`, `obtain` the triple-conjunction from `hex.choose_spec.choose_spec.choose_spec`, and close with `(posIdxFromBisection_congr/negIdxFromBisection_congr ‚Ä¶ ).symm`. Zero `sorry`; `lake build Scott1980` (3166 jobs) clean. `#print axioms` on all four new declarations gives `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}` (inherited from `posIdxFromBisection`/`negIdxFromBisection`'s own `Classical.choose`-based deciders plus `splitFromBisection`'s own fresh `Classical.choose` on the presentation-triple existential, no unexpected leak).

#### Exercise 8.12(e)(d): instantiate for `U`‚Üî`V` ‚Äî `splitX812e`, the exercise's literal target
* **Mathematical Target:** `splitX812e := splitFromBisection UComputablePresentation (U's `IsComputableDiff`) B812e`, where `B812e : ComputableBisection VComputablePresentation` packages a computable canonical bisection for `V`, and
  - `theorem isComputableSplit_812e : IsComputableSplit UComputablePresentation VComputablePresentation splitX812e`, via `isComputableSplit_ofBisection` fed `U_isPositive`/`U_noMinimal`/`U`'s diff-closedness
* **Lean File:** ‚Äî (not yet started); umbrella ‚Äî see sub-rows **8.12(e)(d)(i)‚Äì(iii)** below
* **Proof Notes:** **Re-scoping investigation (2026-07-05), before writing any code, tracing what `ComputableBisection`'s `left_congr`/`right_congr` fields actually demand of `(e)(b)`'s `splitVLeft`/`splitVRight`.** Result: **`left_congr`/`right_congr` are false for `splitVLeft`/`splitVRight` as currently defined** ‚Äî the "expected free... but must be checked" hope flagged back in `(e)(a)`'s own docstring turns out not to hold, and this is a genuine mathematical gap, not a bookkeeping one. **Concrete counterexample**: `V`'s codes are highly non-canonical ‚Äî a fixed set is presentable at *any* sufficiently fine level via repeated `myUpsample` (`canonIdx` never collapses across levels, only handling the "empty ‚Üí master" case), and `splitVLeft`'s output is a full residue class *at the input's own level*, not at any level-independent invariant. Take `X = evens`: presented at `(k, m) = (1, 1)`, `splitVLeft` returns `Y = levelSet 2 1 = {n ‚â° 0 mod 4} = \{0,4,8,12,‚Ä¶\}`; presented at `(k, m) = (2, 5)` (`5 = myUpsample 1 2 1`, the *same set* `evens`, merely upsampled once), `splitVLeft` returns `Y' = levelSet 3 1 = {n ‚â° 0 mod 8} = \{0,8,16,24,‚Ä¶\}`. `Y ‚âÝ Y'` (e.g. `4 ‚àà Y \setminus Y'`) despite both codes presenting the identical `VX`-set. The raw splitting *bit* `‚Ñì‚ÇÄ` genuinely is presentation-invariant (it always equals `min X`, since upsampling only ever adds duplicate copies at *higher* bit positions, never disturbing the least one) ‚Äî the failure is entirely in the *level* `k+1` used as the residue-class modulus, which is not intrinsic to the set `X`, only to the presentation. **Fix**: canonicalize to the *minimal* level at which a set is genuinely periodic before bisecting ‚Äî intrinsic to the set, hence presentation-independent ‚Äî rather than `canonIdx n`'s raw (possibly non-minimal) level. This is a substantial new piece of mathematics (finding the true period of a mask, proving primitive-recursiveness, and ‚Äî the crux ‚Äî proving *uniqueness* of the minimal presentation), comparable in scope to all of `(e)(b)` combined, not a quick fix; deliberately **not** folded into `canonIdx`/`VX` themselves (which are already `Pass` and load-bearing for the rest of the codebase) ‚Äî kept as new, separate infrastructure used only by the bisection construction.
* **Sub-part breakdown:** 3 sequential sub-goals, `(e)(d)(i)`‚Äì`(iii)` below.

##### Exercise 8.12(e)(d)(i): minimal-level canonicalization for `V`'s codes
* **Mathematical Target:** a presentation-independent canonical `(level, mask)` pair for any `levelSet k m`:
  - `def isPeriodicMask (k j m : ‚Ñï) : ‚Ñï` (`{0,1}`-valued) ‚Äî decides whether `levelSet k m` is also presentable at level `j ‚â§ k`, via the canonical witness `myModPow2 m (2 ^ j)` (`m`'s own low bits)
  - `def minLevel (k m : ‚Ñï) : ‚Ñï` ‚Äî the smallest `j ‚â§ k` with `isPeriodicMask k j m = 1`
  - `def minMask (k m : ‚Ñï) : ‚Ñï := myModPow2 m (2 ^ minLevel k m)`
  - `theorem primrec_minLevel`/`primrec_minMask : Nat.Primrec ‚Ä¶`
  - `theorem levelSet_minLevel (k m : ‚Ñï) : levelSet (minLevel k m) (minMask k m) = levelSet k m`
  - `theorem minLevel_unique {k‚ÇÅ m‚ÇÅ k‚ÇÇ m‚ÇÇ : ‚Ñï} (h : levelSet k‚ÇÅ m‚ÇÅ = levelSet k‚ÇÇ m‚ÇÇ) : minLevel k‚ÇÅ m‚ÇÅ = minLevel k‚ÇÇ m‚ÇÇ ‚àß minMask k‚ÇÅ m‚ÇÅ = minMask k‚ÇÇ m‚ÇÇ` ‚Äî the crux fact that actually delivers `left_congr`/`right_congr` in `(e)(d)(ii)`
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/MinLevel.lean` (new file, imports only `LevelSetPrimrec.lean`)
* **Proof Notes:** landed close to the re-scoping plan, with one load-bearing correction and one genuine simplification found while working it out. **Correction**: the plan's periodicity modulus was off by an exponent ‚Äî `levelSet k m` reads `m.testBit (n % 2^k)`, so the *meaningful* truncation of a level-`k` mask is `myModPow2 m (2^k) = m % 2^(2^k)` (matching `myUpsample_lt`'s own `< 2^(2^k')` bound), not `m % 2^k` as the draft assumed; every mask truncation below uses this corrected scale throughout. **Simplification**: rather than the drafted "bounded `‚àÄ i < 2^k` periodicity check" (an `O(2^k)`-body decidable predicate needing its own new bounded-quantifier infrastructure) plus a `max k‚ÇÅ k‚ÇÇ`/strong-induction uniqueness argument, `isPeriodicMask k j m` is instead an *`O(1)` formula* ‚Äî compare `myUpsample j k (myModPow2 m (2^j))` (upsampling `m`'s own low bits back up) against `myModPow2 m (2^k)` (`m`'s own bits at its home level), via the standard `isZero`-of-two-sided-truncated-subtraction equality decider (`Exercise724.lean`'s idiom) ‚Äî reusing already-`Pass` `myUpsample`/`myModPow2` wholesale instead of building new quantifier machinery. Its defining correctness fact, `isPeriodicMask_iff : isPeriodicMask k j m = 1 ‚Üî levelSet k m = levelSet j m` (for `j ‚â§ k`), falls out of two already-`Pass` facts alone ‚Äî `levelSet_myUpsample` and `levelSet_inj_of_lt` (`LevelSetPrimrec.lean`) ‚Äî with no new induction. `minLevel`/`minMask` are the exact `myFirstBit` (`SplitV.lean`) bounded-`Nat.rec`-fold idiom transplanted verbatim (test `isPeriodicMask k i m` in place of `myTestBit m i`, base case `j = k` always available via `isPeriodicMask_self`); `primrec_minLevel`'s only wrinkle versus `primrec_myFirstBit` is that the "fixed parameter" threaded through `Nat.Primrec.prec` is the *pair* `pair k m` rather than a single `m`, requiring one extra `unpair.1.unpair.1`/`unpair.1.unpair.2` layer throughout ‚Äî otherwise identical. **The crux, `minLevel_unique`**, ended up *not* needing the drafted `max k‚ÇÅ k‚ÇÇ`/strong-induction machinery at all ‚Äî it reduces to one new elementary lemma, `levelSet_presentable_imp_self`: *if* `levelSet k m` is presentable at some level `j ‚â§ k` via **any** witness mask `m'` at all, it is already presentable there via the canonical witness `myModPow2 m (2^j)` built from `m` alone. Proved by two direct specializations of `levelSet j m' = levelSet k m`'s `Set.ext_iff` unfolding ‚Äî once at `n = i` and once at `n = i % 2^j`, for a fixed bit position `i < 2^k` ‚Äî which pin down `m.testBit i = m.testBit (i % 2^j)` by pure substitution, no induction whatsoever (the two specializations' `(i % 2^k)`/`((i%2^j)%2^k)` mod-arithmetic collapse to `i` and `i % 2^j` respectively via `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt`, then the two equations chain directly). With this lemma in hand, `minLevel_eq`/`minMask_eq` are a short `by_contra`/trichotomy argument (two minimal witnesses of the same presentability predicate, one strictly below the other, contradicts the smaller one's own minimality ‚Äî mirroring `myFirstBit_spec`'s own "no smaller witness" clause) plus one final `levelSet_inj_of_lt` call for the mask. Zero `sorry`; `lake build Scott1980` (2986 jobs for this file alone, 3167 for the whole project) clean. `#print axioms` on `minLevel_unique`/`minLevel_eq`/`minMask_eq`/`levelSet_minLevel`/`primrec_minLevel`/`primrec_minMask`/`isPeriodicMask_iff`/`levelSet_presentable_imp_self` gives `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}` throughout (the same inherited `Nat`-order/decidability footprint documented project-wide, no fresh leak ‚Äî this file introduces no `Classical.choice`/`Exists.choose` of its own).

Fixed by replacing `congr 1` with the more surgical `apply congrArg (levelSet (splitVMinLevel n + 1))`, which fixes the first argument outright (no unification search) and reduces directly to the mask-equality goal ‚Äî no `@[irreducible]` needed, unlike the `Recursive.lean`-era instances of this pitfall, since here the fix is purely tactic-level (avoid `congr`'s general-purpose unification path entirely rather than blocking unfolding). #### Exercise 8.12(g)(3)
* **Mathematical Target:** `SplitSpec' V splitX812e` and `SplitSpec' U splitX812f` ‚Äî the `Prop`-only, set-level splitting contract that `(c)`'s abstract `xStep`/`yStep`/`DomainIso` machinery (and hence `(d)`'s `effectiveIso812d`) actually consumes, for the two concrete splits built in `(e)`/`(f)`
* **Lean File:** `Exercise812d.lean` (`IsComputableSplit` redesign), `Exercise812e.lean` (`splitFromBisection` redesign + `splitFromBisection_isSplitSpec'`), `Exercise812eD.lean` (`hxSplit812e`), `Exercise812f.lean` (`hySplit812f`) ‚Äî **complete in full as of 2026-07-06 (part 3)**
* **Proof Notes:** **2026-07-06 (part 1): confirmed `SplitSpec' V splitX812e` FALSE as originally architected** ‚Äî full argument below, superseded by part 2's repair. **2026-07-06 (part 2): repaired the root cause identified in part 1**, exactly option (a) flagged at the end of part 1 (`IsComputableSplit.posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec` weakened to be conditional on non-emptiness, then the change propagated through every consumer). This unblocks the *design* ‚Äî `IsComputableSplit` and `SplitSpec'` are no longer structurally incompatible ‚Äî but does **not** by itself produce a `SplitSpec'`-satisfying concrete split: `splitFromBisection` (`Exercise812e.lean`) still unconditionally returns `Q.X m` (never literally `‚àÖ`) on both branches whenever a decider fires, so `SplitSpec' V splitX812e` is *still* not proved (nor provable as `splitFromBisection` is currently defined) ‚Äî that half of `(g)(3)` remains open, now as a tractable, unblocked task rather than an impossible one. Part 1's original argument, for the record:
  1. `splitX812e := ComputableBisection.splitFromBisection UComputablePresentation U_isComputableDiff B812e`. Its two outputs were, by `IsComputableSplit`'s *original, unconditional* contract (`posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec`, `Exercise812d.lean` `(d)(2)`), *always* literally `Q.X (posIdxFromBisection ‚Ä¶)` / `Q.X (negIdxFromBisection ‚Ä¶)` where `Q := VComputablePresentation`.
  2. `Q.X j` is **never `‚àÖ`, for any `j`** ‚Äî `Q.mem_X : ‚àÄ n, V.mem (Q.X n)` and `V.mem X := ‚àÉ k m, X = levelSet k m ‚àß X.Nonempty` (`Exercise812.lean` line 199) structurally *requires* nonempty; the mirror fact holds for `U`/`UComputablePresentation` (`U.mem X := ‚Ä¶ ‚àß X.Nonempty ‚àß ‚Ä¶`, `Definition87.lean` line 96).
  3. `posIdxFromBisection`/`negIdxFromBisection` (`Exercise812e.lean`) *by design* both evaluate to `m` (i.e. literally `B` itself, not `‚àÖ`) whenever **either** `emptyInterDec`/`emptyDiffDec` fires.
  4. Concretely: whenever `A ‚à© Xn = ‚àÖ` while `B ‚âÝ ‚àÖ` (routine and unavoidable), `SplitSpec'` demands `(splitX812e A B Xn).1 = ‚àÖ`, but by (1)‚Äì(3) the actual value was `Q.X m = B ‚âÝ ‚àÖ`. A genuine contradiction under the *original* unconditional `posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec`.
  5. Not sidesteppable by supplying a *different* already-available split: `effectiveIso812d`/`domainIsoCode812d` (`Exercise812d.lean` `(d)(6)`) bind `hxSplit : SplitSpec' D‚ÇÅ splitX` to the **same** `splitX` as `hSplitX : IsComputableSplit P‚ÇÄ P‚ÇÅ splitX`, and the choice-based `splitChoice'` (`Exercise812c.lean`) satisfies `SplitSpec'` but cannot satisfy `IsComputableSplit` (not primitive recursive).
  6. **The repair (part 2):** weakened `IsComputableSplit.posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec` from unconditional `(split ‚Ä¶).1 = Q.X (posIdx ‚Ä¶)` to conditional `(split ‚Ä¶).1 ‚âÝ ‚àÖ ‚Üí (split ‚Ä¶).1 = Q.X (posIdx ‚Ä¶)` (symmetrically for `negIdx_spec`/`.2`) ‚Äî exactly the fix sketched in part 1's root-cause note. Propagated through `Exercise812d.lean`: `posIdx_mem`/`negIdx_mem` corollaries gained the same `hne` hypothesis; `xSubStep_correct`/`ySubStep_correct` (`(d)(3)(b)`) now derive the needed non-emptiness from `SplitSpec'`'s own "empty iff empty" conjunct plus `emptyInterDec_eq_one_iff`/`emptyDiffDec_eq_one_iff` (needing `atomPairG_invariant`-style `hAB`/`hBmem` preconditions threaded in from every call site) before invoking `posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec`, rather than getting the equality for free; the same pattern (derive `‚âÝ ‚àÖ` from the junk-flag being `0` via `selectFn_one_eq_zero_iff` + the relevant `*Dec_eq_one_iff`, then feed `SplitSpec'`'s `.2.2.1`/`.2.2.2.1` conjunct) recurs through `atomPairCodeState_correct`, `xPseqAtomIdx_subset_atomPairIdx1`, `xPseqAtomIdx_eq_inter_XPseqCode`, `yPseqAtomIdx_subset_xStepGFst`, `xStepG_snd_eq_inter_XPseqCode`, and `yStepG_fst_eq_inter_YPseqCode`'s closed forms (`(d)(5)`) ‚Äî a genuinely mechanical but *wide* ripple (every call site of the three theorems needed the extra hypotheses threaded through explicitly, since Lean's `include`-based implicit-argument mechanism only auto-supplies section variables *within* the section that declares them, not across section boundaries at a call site). `Exercise812e.lean`'s `isComputableSplit_ofBisection` updated to match (`posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec` fields now take an unused `_hne` parameter).
  7. **The concrete construction (part 3, 2026-07-06): `splitFromBisection` itself redesigned.** Key realization: `posIdxFromBisection`/`negIdxFromBisection` (the *index*-level `‚Ñï`-valued functions) needed **no change at all** ‚Äî they already compute exactly the right index in the "genuinely nonempty" branch of each field and an unread junk placeholder (`m`) in the "should be `‚àÖ`" branch. The bug was purely that `splitFromBisection` (the *set*-level function) wrapped **both** branches in `Q.X (‚ãØ)`, which is never literally `‚àÖ`. Fix: route the same two deciders through a three-way `if`/`else if`/`else` directly at the `Set Œ≥ √ó Set Œ≥` level ‚Äî `emptyInterDec` fires ‚üπ `(‚àÖ, B')`; else `emptyDiffDec` fires ‚üπ `(B', ‚àÖ)`; else the genuine bisection `(Q.X (B.left m), Q.X (B.right m))` ‚Äî proved well-defined (independent of which witness `Classical.choose` picks for the "presented" existential) via a new bridging lemma `splitFromBisection_eq` (built from `emptyInterDec_congr`/`emptyDiffDec_congr`/`B.left_congr`/`B.right_congr`, the same congruence lemmas `(e)(c)(i)` already supplied). Also generalized the previous "not presented ‚Üí junk `(B', B')`" fallback (provably wrong in general: `.1 ‚à© .2 = B' ‚à© B' = B'`, not `‚àÖ`, unless `B' = ‚àÖ`) to the classical `splitChoice'` (`Exercise812c.lean`) ‚Äî needed since `SplitSpec'` is stated for **every** `A`/`Xn : Set Œ±`, not just presented ones, but only free to change since `IsComputableSplit`'s own `posIdx_spec`/`negIdx_spec` only ever constrain the presented case. `splitFromBisection` gained one new parameter, `hWnomin : W.NoMinimal` (needed to build the `splitChoice'` fallback), threaded through `isComputableSplit_ofBisection` and the concrete instantiations (`Exercise812eD.lean`'s `V_noMinimal`, `Exercise812f.lean`'s `U_noMinimal`). The new `splitFromBisection_isSplitSpec'` theorem needs exactly one hypothesis beyond `isComputableSplit_ofBisection`'s own: `hQne : ‚àÄ j, Q.X j ‚âÝ ‚àÖ`, used **only** in the "neither decider fires" branch (to show the bisection's two halves are each individually non-empty, matching `A ‚à© Xn ‚âÝ ‚àÖ ‚Üî .1 ‚âÝ ‚àÖ`/`A \ Xn ‚âÝ ‚àÖ ‚Üî .2 ‚âÝ ‚àÖ`) ‚Äî not derivable from `ComputableBisection`'s abstract fields alone (nothing there rules out `Q.X (B.left m) = ‚àÖ` for an arbitrary `W`), but immediate for both concrete systems from step 2's "`Q.X j` never `‚àÖ`" fact (`fun j => (VX_nonempty j).ne_empty` for `V`, `fun j => (U_mem_UX j).2.1.ne_empty` for `U`). The two decider-fires branches need no such hypothesis at all ‚Äî `.1`/`.2` there are literally `‚àÖ`/`B'`, and the requisite `‚Üî`s reduce to `hAB` via the algebraic facts `A ‚à© Xn = ‚àÖ ‚Üí A \ Xn = A` (resp. `A \ Xn = ‚àÖ ‚Üí A ‚à© Xn = A`). Concrete instances: `hxSplit812e : SplitSpec' V splitX812e` (`Exercise812eD.lean`) and `hySplit812f : SplitSpec' U splitX812f` (`Exercise812f.lean`), each a direct application of `splitFromBisection_isSplitSpec'` fed the relevant `NoMinimal`/`IsPositive`/`DiffClosed` facts plus the nonemptiness closure. `lake build` (3175 jobs) clean, zero `sorry` project-wide; `#print axioms` on `hxSplit812e`/`hySplit812f`/`splitFromBisection_isSplitSpec'` all give `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}` (`Classical.choice` pre-existing throughout this file's `open scoped Classical` ‚Äî not a new leak).

#### Exercise 8.13
* **Mathematical Target:** (logicians) Prove `U` is isomorphic to the domain of all proper filters of the free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators (= the Lindenbaum algebra of propositional calculus). (topologists) Connect this representation of `U` with the collection of non-empty open subsets of `2^‚Ñï` (Cantor space).
* **Lean File:** ‚Äî (scoping investigation only, 2026-07-06, per this project's discipline for genuinely new pieces; no code written yet); umbrella ‚Äî see sub-rows **8.13(a)‚Äì(c)** below
* **Proof Notes:** **Scoping investigation, done before writing any code (per explicit user request).** This *is* another "monster" in the 8.12 mold ‚Äî genuinely new mathematical infrastructure (`grep`-confirmed: **zero** existing Boolean-algebra/filter/propositional-logic/Cantor-space formalization anywhere in `Scott1980/`) ‚Äî but a key structural discovery makes it *much smaller* than 8.12: **8.13 only asks for a plain isomorphism (`‚âÖ·¥∞`, `DomainIso`), never "effective."** Re-reading `Exercise812c.lean`'s `domainIso812c`/`isomorphic_812c` (the abstract two-sided back-and-forth lemma `8.12(c)` built, `D‚ÇÄ ‚âÖ·¥∞ D‚ÇÅ`) confirms it needs **only** plain `‚Ñï`-indexed enumerations `X : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Set Œ±`, `Y : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Set Œ≤` with `IsPositive`/`DiffClosed`/`NoMinimal`/surjectivity-onto-`mem`/`X 0 = master` ‚Äî **no** `ComputablePresentation`/`Nat.Primrec`/`IsComputableSplit`/`IsComputableDiff`/`IsComputableUnion` anywhere. All of `8.12(d)`‚Äì`(g)` (the huge majority of that exercise's ~4,700 lines) existed *purely* to upgrade `‚âÖ·¥∞` to the effective `‚âÖ·µâ` that `8.12`'s own statement demands ‚Äî machinery `8.13` never needs to touch at all. **Second structural discovery, even more load-bearing: `V` (`Exercise812.lean`'s `levelSet k m := {n | m.testBit (n % 2^k)}`) already *is* (up to a trivial relabelling) the free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators, concretely realized as subsets of `‚Ñï` via "the low-order bits of `n`."** `levelSet k m` is exactly a finite Boolean combination of the `k` independent "bit-`i`" generators (`m`'s bitmask selects which of the `2^k` joint valuations of bits `0..k-1` are included) ‚Äî and since any finite Boolean combination of *arbitrary*-position bit-generators is a finite union of same-`k`-prefix classes (pad to a common `k`, enumerate consistent low-bit patterns), `V`'s "non-empty finite unions of `2^k‚Ñï+‚Ñì`" family is *exactly* the full algebra generated by all bit-generators, not merely a sub-fragment. So `8.13`'s "logicians" half is expected to reduce to: (i) build the *same* combinatorial structure `levelSet`-style but on `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool` (Cantor space) instead of `‚Ñï` ‚Äî call it `Lindenbaum : NeighborhoodSystem (‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool)`, `mem X := ‚àÉ k m, X = cylinderSet k m ‚àß X.Nonempty` with `cylinderSet k m := {x : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool | ‚àÄ i < k, x i = m.testBit i}`, a near-verbatim transcription of `levelSet`/`V`'s existing proofs (`V_no_minimal`, `V.IsPositive`, `DiffClosed`, etc. ‚Äî expected to port with only the ambient-carrier-type changed, `‚Ñï`'s `%`/`testBit` arithmetic mirrored by `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`'s pointwise `i < k` prefix-agreement, likely *easier* since no `canonIdx`/`levelSet_myInter`-style bit-arithmetic normalization is needed for a *plain* isomorphism ‚Äî that normalization exists only to support `V`'s *computable* presentation); (ii) `isomorphic_812c`-style back-and-forth to get `Lindenbaum ‚âÖ·¥∞ V` (expected close to mechanical, likely *easier* than `8.12(c)` itself since both sides are literally the same `(k,m)`-indexed combinatorial family, just living in different carrier types ‚Äî may reduce to a direct order-isomorphism `X ‚Ü¶ cylinderSet`'s inverse of `levelSet`'s own `(k,m)` bookkeeping, sidestepping the general back-and-forth machinery entirely); (iii) compose with the now-`Pass` `effectiveIso812_UV.toDomainIso : U ‚âÖ·¥∞ V` (`Exercise812g4.lean`, `Exercise718.lean`'s `EffectiveIso.toDomainIso`) to conclude `Lindenbaum ‚âÖ·¥∞ U`.
  **Open scoping decision (needs user input before starting code):** how far to push the "= Lindenbaum algebra of propositional calculus" identification literally. **Option A (semantic, smaller):** define the Lindenbaum algebra *directly* as (the quotient of) `Formula ‚Ñï` (a small inductive AST ‚Äî `var n`/`‚ä§`/`‚ä•`/`¬¨`/`‚àß`/`‚à®` ‚Äî over countably many propositional variables) by **semantic** equivalence (`œÜ ~ œà := ‚àÄ v : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool, eval v œÜ = eval v œà`), justified by soundness+completeness of classical propositional logic (a standard fact, not reproved) identifying semantic equivalence with provable equivalence ‚Äî then show `[œÜ] ‚Ü¶ {v : eval v œÜ = true}` is a Boolean-algebra isomorphism onto `Lindenbaum`'s underlying algebra. Modest addition (`Formula`/`eval` is a short inductive + recursive `Bool`-eval, no proof calculus needed). **Option B (syntactic, much larger):** build an actual Hilbert-style (or natural-deduction) proof system for propositional logic with `‚ä¢`, then prove soundness *and* completeness w.r.t. `eval`, *then* define the Lindenbaum algebra as the genuine syntactic quotient by `‚ä¢`-provable-equivalence. This is effectively a full propositional-logic metatheory formalization ‚Äî likely bigger than `8.12` on its own ‚Äî and Option A already delivers the *same* final algebra (by the completeness theorem Option B would have to prove anyway) with none of the added machinery. **Recommend Option A** unless the user specifically wants the proof-theoretic development as its own exercise.
  **Topologists' half ‚Äî a genuine finding, not yet a plan:** the literal reading "`Lindenbaum.Element` (proper filters) `‚âÉo` non-empty open subsets of `2^‚Ñï`" is **false** as stated, for a structural reason worth recording: every `Element` (Scott filter) contains `V.master`/`Lindenbaum.master` (`Element.master_mem` is a required field, `Basic.lean` line 216), so the naive map `x ‚Ü¶ ‚ãÉ {X : x.mem X}` is constant (always the whole space) ‚Äî filters do **not** correspond to open sets via *union*. Working out the correct correspondence (via the *opposite* direction, `x ‚Ü¶ ‚ãÇ {X : x.mem X}`, using that basic neighbourhoods are clopen in a *compact* space): this **does** biject `Element` with non-empty **closed** sets that are intersections of clopens (all of them, in a zero-dimensional compact space) ‚Äî order-*reversing* (`x ‚â§ y ‚Üî Z(y) ‚äÜ Z(x)`), proved via a genuine finite-intersection-property/compactness argument (`Z(x) ‚äÜ X ‚Üí X ‚àà x`, for `X` a basic neighbourhood, via extracting a finite subcover of `X`'s complement from `x`'s "witnessing" family and closing under `x`'s existing finite-meet/upward closure ‚Äî a real two-line-of-math but not-yet-formalized argument). This exactly reflects `8.12`'s own aside ("compact = principal"): the **compact/principal** elements are precisely the ones whose `Z(x)` is clopen (hence open), matching `Definition 1.7`'s `principal X ‚Ü¶ X` on the nose; *general* (non-compact) elements correspond to closed, not open, sets. Two live options for what to actually formalize: **(i)** the precise closed-set duality above (mathematically the "real" content, but doesn't literally match "open subsets" as worded ‚Äî would need dualizing via complementation, which turns "non-empty" into "proper" and vice-versa, so *still* doesn't literally match); **(ii)** a much more modest (and easily achievable) reading: show `Lindenbaum`'s basic neighbourhoods (`cylinderSet`) are exactly the clopen basis generating Mathlib's standard product topology on `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool` (`Pi.topologicalSpace`/discrete `Bool` factors) ‚Äî i.e. literally exhibit `{X | Lindenbaum.mem X} ‚à™ {‚àÖ}` as `IsTopologicalBasis` for that topology ‚Äî connecting the algebraic (`ùíü`) and topological (open sets = arbitrary unions of `ùíü`) pictures without a false isomorphism claim. **Needs a user decision before any code is written** (see `HANDOFF.md`'s matching checkpoint / the chat where this was scoped).

#### Exercise 8.13(a)
* **Mathematical Target:** `V` (`Exercise812.lean`) *is* the domain of proper filters of the free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` (independent) generators; hence `U ‚âÖ·¥∞` that domain
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813a.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** Landed **simpler than even the already-optimistic scoping estimate**: no new `NeighborhoodSystem` was needed at all ‚Äî `V` itself (on `‚Ñï`, not `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`) already *is* the algebra, avoiding every bit of `cylinderSet`/Cantor-space bookkeeping the scoping row anticipated. Content: `generator i := {n | n.testBit i}` (the `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators); `GeneratedBy generator` (a small hand-rolled inductive ‚Äî `of`/`univ`/`inter`/`union`/`compl` ‚Äî the Boolean subalgebra of `Set ‚Ñï` they generate, since no such generic notion exists in Mathlib or this project); the headline lemma `V_mem_iff_generatedBy : V.mem X ‚Üî GeneratedBy generator X ‚àß X.Nonempty` (soundness via structural induction on `GeneratedBy`, reusing `V_union_mem`/`levelSet_inter` for the `union`/`inter` cases and a new `levelSet_compl` for the `compl` case; completeness via `levelSet_eq_biUnion` decomposing into `affine`-pieces, each a finite intersection of generators/complements via a new `affine_eq_biInter`, reassembled by `Finset.induction_on`); `generators_independent` (every finite Boolean combination of finitely many generators is non-empty ‚Äî the standard characterization of "freely generates a Boolean algebra," witnessed directly by `bitmaskOf`). Since `Basic.lean`'s `Element` (upward-closed, finite-meet-closed, contains master, and ‚Äî because `V.mem` excludes `‚àÖ` ‚Äî never contains bottom) is *definitionally* "proper filter of `{X | GeneratedBy generator X}`" once `V_mem_iff_generatedBy` is in hand, `V.Element` **is** the domain of proper filters of the free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators, with zero further translation needed. The headline `exercise813a : U ‚âÖ·¥∞ V` is then literally `‚ü®effectiveIso812_UV.toDomainIso‚ü©` (already `Pass`, `Exercise812g4.lean`) ‚Äî no new back-and-forth argument, exactly as the parent row predicted. New arithmetic lemmas needed along the way (none existed in Mathlib): `testBit_mod_two_pow` (`(n % 2^k).testBit i = decide (i<k) && n.testBit i`, via `Nat.testBit_two_pow_mul_add` fed `Nat.div_add_mod`) and `testBit_sum_two_pow`/`bitmaskOf` (read off a prescribed finite bit-pattern, via `Finset.toFinset_bitIndices_sum_two_pow`, generalizing the same trick `Exercise812.lean`'s `upsample` already used once). `lake build` (3176 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; `#print axioms exercise813a`/`V_mem_iff_generatedBy`/`generators_independent` all `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}`, the same pre-existing baseline as every other fact about `V`/`U` in this project.

#### Exercise 8.13(b)
* **Mathematical Target:** Justify the "`= Lindenbaum algebra of propositional calculus`" identification: a `Formula`/propositional-syntax bridge from `8.13(a)`'s concrete `{X | GeneratedBy generator X}` to an actual quotient of propositional formulas
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813b.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** Implemented "Option A" (semantic-equivalence quotient, no full proof calculus/soundness/completeness needed). `Formula` (a minimal `var`/`bot`/`top`/`neg`/`and`/`or` AST over `‚Ñï`-indexed variables) with two parallel recursions: `evalV : (‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool) ‚Üí Formula ‚Üí Bool` (standard truth-valuation semantics) and `evalSet : Formula ‚Üí Set ‚Ñï` (the same recursion, but interpreting `var i ‚Ü¶ generator i` and Boolean connectives as `Set ‚Ñï` operations ‚Äî i.e. `8.13(a)`'s specific homomorphism). `mem_evalSet_iff : n ‚àà evalSet œÜ ‚Üî evalV (fun i => n.testBit i) œÜ = true` is the bridge between them (structural induction, `simp`-only); from it, `generatedBy_iff_exists_evalSet` shows `evalSet`'s range is exactly `GeneratedBy generator` (both directions by induction, `of`/`univ`/`inter`/`union`/`compl` matching `Formula`'s constructors one-for-one). The one substantive lemma is `semanticEquiv_iff_evalSet_eq`: `SemanticEquiv œÜ œà` (`‚àÄ v, evalV v œÜ = evalV v œà` ‚Äî Scott's own Lindenbaum equivalence, quantifying over *all* valuations `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`) agrees with `evalSet œÜ = evalSet œà` (which only ever "tests" the countably many *bit-derived* valuations `n ‚Ü¶ (fun i => n.testBit i)`) ‚Äî true because any single formula only mentions finitely many variables (`vars : Formula ‚Üí Finset ‚Ñï`, `evalV_eq_of_agree`), so any arbitrary valuation can be swapped for a matching bit-derived one on that finite set, witnessed directly via `bitmaskOf` (`exists_bitsOf_agree`, reusing `8.13(a)`'s `testBit_bitmaskOf`). `Lindenbaum := Quotient formulaSetoid` is then literally *the Lindenbaum algebra of propositional calculus* as a type; `Lindenbaum.toSet := Quotient.lift evalSet ...` is well-defined by the ‚ü∏ direction above, `Lindenbaum.toSet_injective` by the ‚üπ direction (`Quotient.sound`), and `Lindenbaum.range_toSet : Set.range toSet = {X | GeneratedBy generator X}` (‚üπ `generatedBy_iff_exists_evalSet`) makes `Lindenbaum ‚âÉ {X // GeneratedBy generator X}` explicit ‚Äî i.e. `8.13`'s parenthetical, "free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ`-generators (= Lindenbaum algebra of propositional calculus)," is now a proved bijection, not an assertion. Bonus: `Entails`/`entails_iff_evalSet_subset` (via the identical finitary argument) shows the bijection also matches semantic entailment with `‚äÜ`, i.e. it respects order/the Boolean-algebra structure, not just underlying sets ‚Äî without needing to bundle a full `BooleanAlgebra Lindenbaum` instance (would need ~10+ axiom lemmas, judged disproportionate to this exercise's actual ask). `lake build` (3177 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; `#print axioms` on `Lindenbaum.toSet_injective`/`Lindenbaum.range_toSet`/`semanticEquiv_iff_evalSet_eq`/`entails_iff_evalSet_subset` all `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}` ‚Äî confirmed (by comparison to `#print axioms exercise813a`) the same pre-existing baseline inherited transitively from `8.13(a)`/`8.12`'s `‚âÖ·¥∞` chain, not anything new introduced here.

#### Exercise 8.13(c)
* **Mathematical Target:** (topologists) Connect `8.13(a)`'s filter-domain representation of `U` with the non-empty open subsets of Cantor space `2^‚Ñï` (`‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool` with the product topology)
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813c.lean` (umbrella; user chose the "full Stone duality" scope over the more modest `IsTopologicalBasis`-only reading ‚Äî see sub-rows **8.13(c1)‚Äì(c4)** below, all now **Pass**)
* **Proof Notes:** The literal "proper filters `‚âÉo` non-empty opens" reading is **false** (every filter contains `master`, so `‚ãÉ`-of-filter is constant; filters correspond, order-*reversingly*, to non-empty **closed** sets via `x ‚Ü¶ ‚ãÇ{X : x.mem X}`, using compactness). The reading that actually lands on "opens" (matching Scott's literal word) goes through the *dual* notion ‚Äî **ideals** (downward-closed, finite-join-closed, proper) ‚Äî since `‚ãÉ`-of-an-ideal-of-clopens is open (not constant), and `Y ‚Ü¶ Y·∂ú` is a Boolean-algebra anti-automorphism turning ideals into filters. Full chain, decomposed into four subgoals: **(c1)** Cantor space's clopen algebra is exactly `GeneratedBy genPoint` (a literal transcription of `8.13(a)`'s `generator`/`GeneratedBy generator`, but on carrier `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool` via coordinate-projections `genPoint i := {x | x i = true}`), using compactness + `Mathlib`'s `isTopologicalBasis_pi`/`isTopologicalBasis_singletons` for the (harder) "every clopen is `GeneratedBy genPoint`" direction; opens are then unions of such clopens. **(c2)** `generator`(on `‚Ñï`)/`genPoint`(on `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`) realize the *same* abstract free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators ‚Äî made precise, with zero new independence argument, by reusing `8.13(b)`'s `Formula`/`Lindenbaum` quotient with a second evaluation `evalSet' : Formula ‚Üí Set (‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool)` (`var i ‚Ü¶ genPoint i`), giving `Lindenbaum ‚âÉ {X | GeneratedBy generator X}` and `Lindenbaum ‚âÉ {Y | GeneratedBy genPoint Y}` simultaneously, hence (composing) an explicit order-isomorphism between the two concrete algebras *without* needing any bijection of the (very different ‚Äî countable vs. uncountable) underlying carriers `‚Ñï`/`‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`. **(c3)** general small lemma: for a Boolean subalgebra of sets closed under complement, `I` is a proper ideal iff `{Y·∂ú : Y ‚àà I}` is a proper filter ‚Äî applied to Cantor clopens. **(c4)** assembly: non-empty open `O ‚Ü¶ idealOf O := {Y | GeneratedBy genPoint Y ‚àß Y ‚äÜ O}` (an ideal by (c1)'s clopen-algebra structure, with `‚ãÉ idealOf O = O` since clopens form a basis) `‚Ü¶` (c3) dual filter of Cantor clopens `‚Ü¶` (c2) filter of `‚Ñï`-clopens `= V.Element ‚Ü¶` (`8.13a`) element of `U`. Sub-rows below track (c1)‚Äì(c4) individually; not all need to land in the same Lean file. `8.13(c)`, like `(b)`, remains independently optional ‚Äî `8.13`'s mathematical content is already `Pass` via `(a)`+`(b)` ‚Äî this is purely the topologists' expository half.

#### Exercise 8.13(c1)
* **Mathematical Target:** Cantor space `2^‚Ñï`'s clopen algebra is exactly `GeneratedBy genPoint` (`genPoint i := {x : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool | x i = true}`), and every open set is a union of such clopens
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813c.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** `genPoint i := (fun x => x i) ‚Åª¬π' {true}` ‚Äî literal transcription of `8.13(a)`'s `generator i` onto carrier `‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`; `isClopen_genPoint` via `isClopen_discrete {true}` (`Bool`'s `DiscreteTopology`) `.preimage (continuous_apply i)`. **Easy direction** `generatedBy_genPoint_isClopen`: clopens closed under `GeneratedBy`'s ops, plain structural induction. **Hard direction** (the headline, `isClopen_iff_generatedBy_genPoint`): every clopen `Y` is `GeneratedBy genPoint`, via compactness ‚Äî `box I f := {x | ‚àÄ i‚ààI, x i = f i}` (finite-support basis element); `isOpen_pi_iff` gives, for each `f ‚àà Y`, a finite `I` with `box I f ‚äÜ Y` (shrinking `u i` to `{f i}`, valid since `Bool` is discrete so any set containing `f i` works and `f i ‚àà u i}` already given); each `box` is `GeneratedBy genPoint` (`generatedBy_genPoint_box`, `Finset.induction_on` + case-split on `f a`, mirroring `8.13(a)`'s `generatedBy_affine`); `Y` clopen ‚üπ compact (`IsClosed.isCompact`, `CompactSpace (‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool)` free from `Bool`'s finiteness + Tychonoff) extracts a **finite** subcover (`IsCompact.elim_finite_subcover`) of `box`es all `‚äÜ Y`, so `Y` = their union, `GeneratedBy genPoint` by `generatedBy_genPoint_biUnion` (`Finset.set_biUnion_insert` idiom, same as `8.13(a)`'s `generatedBy_biUnion_affine`; needed `classical` for a generic-`Œ≤` `DecidableEq` instance). Corollary `isOpen_iff_exists_iUnion_generatedBy`: opens (not just clopens) are exactly unions of `GeneratedBy genPoint` sets ‚Äî the "topological basis" content the parent row's more modest candidate `(ii)` would have targeted, now obtained as a free corollary of the fuller clopen identification. `lake build` (3178 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; `#print axioms` on both headline theorems `‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}`, the project's standard baseline.

#### Exercise 8.13(c2)
* **Mathematical Target:** `generator`(`‚Ñï`)/`genPoint`(`‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool`) realize the same abstract free Boolean algebra on `‚Ñµ‚ÇÄ` generators ‚Äî an explicit order-isomorphism `{X | GeneratedBy generator X} ‚âÉo {Y | GeneratedBy genPoint Y}`, mediated by `8.13(b)`'s `Lindenbaum` quotient (a second evaluation `evalSet'`)
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813c.lean` (same file as `(c1)`, new section)
* **Proof Notes:** `evalSet' : Formula ‚Üí Set (‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool)` (`8.13(b)`'s `Formula`, evaluated via `genPoint` instead of `generator`) ‚Äî *simpler* than `evalSet`: `mem_evalSet'_iff` needs no bit-encoding step (`x : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Bool` already *is* a valuation, contrast `evalSet`'s `n ‚Ü¶ fun i => n.testBit i`), so `semanticEquiv_iff_evalSet'_eq`/`entails_iff_evalSet'_subset` need no finitary agreement argument either (both direct `rw`/case-split, no `exists_bitsOf_agree`-style lemma). `generatedBy_iff_exists_evalSet'`, `Lindenbaum.toSet'`/`toSet'_injective`/`range_toSet'` are line-for-line mirrors of `8.13(b)`'s versions. Rather than bundling an explicit `OrderIso` (would need a `PartialOrder Lindenbaum` instance lifting `Entails` to the quotient, judged disproportionate machinery), the headline is the lighter-weight but equally substantive **`Corresponds X Y := ‚àÉ œÜ, evalSet œÜ = X ‚àß evalSet' œÜ = Y`**: witnesses via a common `Formula` that `{X|GeneratedBy generator X}` and `{Y|GeneratedBy genPoint Y}` are the same algebra ‚Äî `exists_corresponds_of_generatedBy_generator`/`_genPoint` (existence both ways, from `generatedBy_iff_exists_evalSet`/`evalSet'`), `Corresponds.unique_left`/`unique_right` (uniqueness both ways, via `semanticEquiv_iff_evalSet_eq`/`evalSet'_eq` composed through `SemanticEquiv`), `Corresponds.subset_iff` (respects `‚äÜ`, via both `entails_iff_evalSet_subset` lemmas) ‚Äî together exactly the data of an order-isomorphism, stated relationally. `lake build` (3178 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; axiom baseline unchanged.

#### Exercise 8.13(c3)
* **Mathematical Target:** For a Boolean subalgebra of sets closed under complement, `I` is a proper ideal iff `{Y·∂ú : Y ‚àà I}` is a proper filter
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813c.lean` (same file as `(c1)`/`(c2)`, new section)
* **Proof Notes:** A `g`-generic toolkit (not Cantor-specific ‚Äî works for any `{Œ± : Type*}`/`g : ‚Ñï ‚Üí Set Œ±`): `dualFilter x := {Y | Y·∂ú ‚àà x}` (`Y ‚Ü¶ Y·∂ú` applied to a whole family; `dualFilter_dualFilter` records it as its own inverse). Rather than bundling `IsIdealOf`/`IsFilterOf` structures, each of the four defining properties is its own small lemma taking exactly the hypothesis it needs, chosen to match `Basic.lean`'s `Element` fields one-for-one so `8.13(c4)` could assemble a literal `V.Element` term directly from them: `generatedBy_of_mem_dualFilter` (membership in `GeneratedBy g` propagates, via `GeneratedBy.compl`), `univ_mem_dualFilter` (an ideal containing `‚àÖ` dualizes to a filter containing `univ`), `not_empty_mem_dualFilter` (an ideal excluding `univ` dualizes to a filter excluding `‚àÖ`), `inter_mem_dualFilter` (join-closed ideal dualizes to meet-closed filter, via `(Y‚à©Z)·∂ú = Y·∂ú‚à™Z·∂ú`), `up_mem_dualFilter` (downward-closed ideal dualizes to upward-closed filter, via `Z‚äÜY ‚Üî Y·∂ú‚äÜZ·∂ú`) ‚Äî each a one-line De Morgan argument. `lake build` (3178 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; axiom baseline unchanged.

#### Exercise 8.13(c4)
* **Mathematical Target:** Assembly: non-empty open `O ‚äÜ 2^‚Ñï ‚Ü¶ idealOf O ‚Ü¶` (c3) dual filter `‚Ü¶` (c2) filter of `‚Ñï`-clopens `= V.Element ‚Ü¶` (`8.13a`) element of `U`
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise813c.lean` (same file as `(c1)`‚Äì`(c3)`, final section)
* **Proof Notes:** `idealOf O := {Y | GeneratedBy genPoint Y ‚àß Y ‚äÜ O}` (the clopens inside `O`) is a proper ideal exactly when `O ‚âÝ Set.univ` (`empty_mem_idealOf`, `univ_not_mem_idealOf`, `union_mem_idealOf`, `down_mem_idealOf`); dualizing (`8.13(c3)`'s toolkit) gives a proper filter of `GeneratedBy genPoint`; three more `Corresponds` helpers (`generatedBy_left/right`, `nonempty_iff` ‚Äî via `n ‚Ü¶ fun i=>n.testBit i` directly for `‚Üí`, `exists_bitsOf_agree` for `‚Üê`, mirroring `8.13(b)`'s finitary argument ‚Äî and `inter`) transport it through `8.13(c2)`'s `Corresponds` to a proper filter of `GeneratedBy generator`; **`elementOfOpen`** assembles this directly as a genuine `V.Element` term (all four `Basic.lean` `Element` fields ‚Äî `sub`/`master_mem`/`inter_mem`/`up_mem` ‚Äî discharged from the toolkit, no new axioms), hence (via `exercise813a`) an element of `U`. **Corrected Scott's own phrasing en route**: "non-empty" is, taken literally, the *wrong* exclusion for this construction ‚Äî `idealOf ‚àÖ = {‚àÖ}` dualizes just fine, to the legitimate (if degenerate) **bottom** element of `U`; what actually breaks properness is `O = Set.univ` (forces the dual filter to contain `‚àÖ`, forbidden by `V_mem_iff_generatedBy`). The precise hypothesis is `O ‚âÝ Set.univ` ("proper"), documented prominently in the file; Scott's remark is informal here, consistent with the parallel "opens vs. closeds" imprecision already flagged in the parent row. `lake build` (3178 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; axiom baseline unchanged.

#### Exercise 8.14
* **Mathematical Target:** *closure operators* (`I‚äëa`); fixed-point set finitary; what are the finite elements
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise814.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** `IsClosureOperator a := IsRetraction a ‚àß idMap E ‚â§ a` (`I_E ‚äë a`, i.e. `a` inflationary ‚Äî `le_toElementMap_of_isClosureOperator`). Main theorem **`isFinitary_of_isClosureOperator`**: for any closure operator `a : E ‚Üí E`, `Fix(a)` (`FixSet a`, from `Theorem85.lean`) is finitary. Strategy: identify the compact elements of `Fix(a)` as exactly `a(‚ÜëX)` for `E`-neighbourhoods `X` (`IsCompactFix`, `isCompactFix_toElementMap_principal` ‚Äî via inflation + `E`'s own `principal_isCompactElt`), show finite bounded joins of compacts are compact (`isCompactFix_sup`, via Exercise 1.27's `sSup`/`le_sSup`/`sSup_le`), then build a genuine `NeighborhoodSystem` **`domainOfClosure`** whose tokens are `CompactFix h` (the compact fixed points) and whose neighbourhoods are principal up-sets `upFix` (smaller compact ‚üπ bigger up-set, matching the information order); `inter_mem` is exactly `upFix_inter` (intersection of two up-sets = up-set of the join). The order isomorphism **`fixSetOrderIso : FixSet a ‚âÉo (domainOfClosure h).Element`** goes via `toElementFilter`/`fromElementFilter` (directed union, over `confirmedIdx`, of all compacts confirmed by a filter), with round-trips `toElementFilter_fromElementFilter`/`fromElementFilter_toElementFilter` ‚Äî the latter using `E`'s algebraicity transported through `a` (`toElementMap_eq_iSupDirected_genFamily`: `y` is the directed union of `a(‚ÜëX)` for `X ‚àà y`, from applying `a` to `eq_iSupDirected_principal`). **Finite elements answered exactly** (`isCompactFix_iff`): `y ‚àà Fix(a)` is compact iff `y = a(‚ÜëX)` for a single `E`-neighbourhood `X` ‚Äî a sandwich argument pulling one witness `X` out of the directed decomposition via compactness. The "give examples on `PN`" prompt is expository and left as an optional non-blocking follow-up (not needed for the exercise's actual imperative). `lake build` (2955 jobs) clean, zero `sorry`; `#print axioms` on `isFinitary_of_isClosureOperator`/`isCompactFix_iff`/`fixSetOrderIso` `‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`, choice-free.

#### Exercise 8.15
* **Mathematical Target:** Give a *direct* proof that `{X ‚à£ X ‚óÅ D}` is effectively presented if `D`
  is. (Hint: the finite elements of the domain correspond exactly to the finite systems `X ‚óÅ D`.)
  For `D = ùí∞`, show the computable elements correspond exactly to the effectively presented domains
  (up to effective isomorphism).
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise815.lean` (complete: both halves done, choice-free
  modulo the pre-existing `UX` artifact; 6g deliberately out of scope, documented in-file)
* **Proof Notes:** direct (non-`Exercise222`) construction. Fix a `ComputablePresentation P` of `D`.
  For a finite index list `js : List ‚Ñï`, the *finitely generated subsystem* `Fin(js) := {Y ‚à£ ‚àÉ sub
  ‚äë js, D.mem Y ‚àß Y = interFrom P D.master sub}` (reusing `Theorem75.lean`'s `interFrom`) is itself a
  subsystem `finGenSys(js) ‚óÅ D` (closure under consistent intersection: combine two sub-selections by
  list-`filter`, no bitmask needed at this layer). The **key algebraic fact**
  (`Fin_concat_le_iff`): for any `D' ‚óÅ D`, `Fin(js‚ÇÅ ++ js‚ÇÇ) ‚äÜ D'.mem ‚Üî Fin(js‚ÇÅ) ‚äÜ D'.mem ‚àß Fin(js‚ÇÇ) ‚äÜ
  D'.mem` ‚Äî proved via `interFrom_mem_of_witness` (any intermediate partial meet along a consistent
  chain is itself consistent, using the *full* meet as the witness) + `D'.inter_closed`. Iterating
  over singletons gives **`Fin_le_iff_forall_mem`**: `Fin(js) ‚äÜ D'.mem ‚Üî ‚àÄ i ‚àà js, D'.mem (P.X i)` ‚Äî
  the workhorse for everything downstream.

  **The domain.** Token type `List ‚Ñï`; `SubD.mem N := ‚àÉ js, N = nbhd(js)` where `nbhd(js) := {js' ‚à£
  Fin(js) ‚äÜ Fin(js')}` (anti-monotone principal up-set, mirroring `Exercise222.nbhd`).
  `nbhd(js‚ÇÅ) ‚à© nbhd(js‚ÇÇ) = nbhd(js‚ÇÅ ++ js‚ÇÇ)` is exactly `Fin_concat_le_iff` instantiated at
  `D' := finGenSys(js')`. `nbhd(a) = nbhd(b) ‚Üî Fin(a) = Fin(b)` (antisymmetry, `a ‚àà nbhd(a)` reflexive).

  **The isomorphism `SubD.Element ‚âÉo {D' ‚à£ D' ‚óÅ D}`** (fully choice-free ‚Äî an improvement on
  `Exercise222`'s classical route!): forward `D' ‚Ü¶ (fun N ‚Ü¶ ‚àÉjs, N=nbhd(js) ‚àß ‚àÄi‚ààjs, D'.mem(P.X i))`;
  backward `x ‚Ü¶ (fun Y ‚Ü¶ ‚àÉjs, x.mem(nbhd js) ‚àß Y ‚àà Fin(js))`. Round trips use `Fin_le_iff_forall_mem`
  plus a finite fold combining witnesses over the (finite) list `js` via repeated `x.inter_mem`
  (concatenating confirmed generators) ‚Äî no need for `Exercise222`'s `Cl`/arbitrary-finite-subset
  machinery or `Classical.choice`.

  **Computability.** `X n := nbhd(decodeList n)`. `cons_computable`/`inter`/`inter_spec` are
  **free**: `nbhd(js‚ÇÅ) ‚à© nbhd(js‚ÇÇ) = nbhd(js‚ÇÅ++js‚ÇÇ)` *exactly* (not just `‚äÜ`), so
  `appendListCode n m` is always a valid (in fact exact) witness/index, no consistency case-split
  needed. Only `interEq_computable` (deciding *equality* `Fin(A)=Fin(B)`) needs real content: a
  "`P.X m ‚àà Fin(decodeList c)`" decider via `Theorem75.lean`'s Milestone 3 apparatus (`bitSelect` +
  a new `idxCharAt` device reusing `consCharAt`'s fold but projecting the index component instead
  of the flag, since that component's update is independent of the flag) bundled through
  `RecDecidable.bExists`/`RecDecidable‚ÇÇ.bForallList` (`Recursive.lean`) to reach `Fin(A)‚äÜFin(B)`,
  then both inclusions via `Set.Subset.antisymm_iff` give equality. `cons_computable`/`inter`/
  `inter_spec` assembled from `SubDX_inter_eq` (exact, unconditional); `masterIdx := encodeList []`.
  Capstone `subsystem_isEffectivelyGiven_of_isEffectivelyGiven`: `D.IsEffectivelyGiven ‚Üí ‚àÉ V,
  V.IsEffectivelyGiven ‚àß Nonempty (V.Element ‚âÉo {D' ‚à£ D' ‚óÅ D})`, combining `SubDPresentation` with
  the `subsystemIso` order isomorphism ‚Äî **the first half of Exercise 8.15, done directly and
  choice-free** (`#print axioms` on every new theorem `‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`).

  **Second half (`D = ùí∞`), Subgoal 6 ‚Äî plan (worked in sequence).** Fix `UP := UComputablePresentation`
  and `x : (SubD UP).Element`; write `D'x := toSubsystemSys UP x` (`D'x ‚óÅ ùí∞` via
  `toSubsystemSys_subsystem`). A key mathematical subtlety, found while planning: for an *arbitrary*
  abstract `Q : ComputablePresentation D'x` unrelated to `UP`, deciding `Q.Xn ‚äÜ UP.Xm` needs a
  cross-presentation comparison that the `ComputablePresentation` axioms do **not** provide (two
  numberings of the same set need not be effectively comparable without extra structure ‚Äî a genuine
  phenomenon, not a gap in this codebase; a disjoint-interval example shows `x.mem(nbhdGen UP js)` does
  **not** imply `ùí∞.mem(interFrom UP ùí∞.master js)` in general, e.g. `js` naming two disjoint rational
  intervals). So the second half is formalized **relative to `UP`'s own enumeration** (the natural,
  provable reading of "up to effective isomorphism"), in sub-subgoals:
  * **6a** ‚úÖ (index-set reduction, `subsystemU_computable_iff_index_set_re`): `IsComputableElement
    (SubDPresentation P) x ‚Üî REPred (fun i => D'x.mem (P.X i))`, via `mem_nbhdGen_iff` +
    `REPred.forall_mem_decodeList` (and its converse, reindexing along the primitive-recursive
    singleton-list code `i ‚Ü¶ encodeList [i]`).
  * **6b‚Äì6d** ‚úÖ (combined into one theorem, `subsystemU_element_computable_iff`): `x` computable ‚Üî
    `‚àÉ r, Nat.Primrec r ‚àß ‚àÄ i, D'x.mem (P.X i) ‚Üî ‚àÉ n, r n = i` ‚Äî `‚Üí` via
    `Exercise714.repred_exists_primrec_range` (witness `a := P.masterIdx`), `‚Üê` via
    `Exercise714.repred_range_primrec`. Both choice-free (`#print axioms ‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`),
    and ‚Äî like Subgoals 1‚Äì5 ‚Äî stated generically in `D`/`P` (never needed `D = ùí∞` specifically).
  * **6e (enumeration half) ‚úÖ.** Specializing to `P := UComputablePresentation` (`D := U`) as planned,
    two `ùí∞`-specific lemmas unlock the construction: **`UX_Uinter_dichotomy`** ‚Äî `UX (Uinter n m) =
    U.master ‚à® UX (Uinter n m) = UX n ‚à© UX m`, *unconditionally* (proved via `canonList`'s filter-`nil`/
    `cons` cases; the fallback triggers exactly when the raw pairwise intersection is empty, since both
    `UX n, UX m ‚äÜ Set.Ico 0 1` already, making the clip a no-op) ‚Äî and **`toSubsystemSys_mem_foldl_Uinter`**
    ‚Äî folding `Uinter` from a `D'x.mem` accumulator along a `D'x.mem`-generator list stays `D'x.mem`, by
    induction combining `finGen` witnesses via `interFrom_append_eq` (true-intersection branch) or
    `D'x.master_mem` (fallback branch). Crucially, **the branch only ever appears inside the *proof*,
    never inside the *definition* of the enumeration** ‚Äî this is exactly what defeats the
    Prop-to-data-extraction obstacle flagged for 6e in the previous checkpoint: `Uinter`'s arithmetic
    unconditionally "does the right thing" (dichotomy), so no data-level case split on a `RecDecidable`
    flag is ever needed. With these in hand: `Q'X r n` folds `Uinter ‚àò r` over the list coded by `n`
    via `Recursive.lean`'s **existing, generic** `foldCode` engine (`Q'Xcode r := foldCode (QstepFn r) 0
    UP.masterIdx`, primitive recursive via the already-proved `primrec_foldCode` ‚Äî no new
    fold-primitive-recursiveness machinery needed). `Q'X_eq` identifies `Q'X r n` with the *generic*
    `Theorem75.idxchain UP (map r (decodeList n))`, giving: **`Q'x_mem_X`** (every `Q'X r n` is
    `D'x.mem`, via `toSubsystemSys_mem_foldl_Uinter`) and **`Q'x_surj`** (every `D'x`-neighbourhood is
    some `Q'X r n`, via the *generic* `idxchain_spec` plus a new choice-free list-level preimage lemma
    `exists_preimage_of_forall_mem`). All choice-free (the `Classical.choice` `#print axioms` shows for
    anything touching `UX` is `Definition87.lean`'s already-documented, pre-existing Mathlib-`‚Ñö`-order
    artifact, confirmed by auditing `U_mem_UX` directly ‚Äî not anything new here).
  * **6e (`inter`/`cons_computable`) ‚úÖ ‚Äî resolved by a binary term algebra.** The obstacle above was a
    *different* problem from the Prop-extraction issue (fully avoided by `Q'X`/`Q'Xcode` being
    directly-defined functions throughout) ‚Äî it was purely arithmetic: **`Uinter`'s fallback is not
    "conservative"**, so list-code concatenation (`Q'inter r n m := encodeList (decodeList n ++
    decodeList m)`) fails `inter_spec`, and the alternative fix (`Uinter (Q'Xcode r n) (Q'Xcode r m)`)
    repairs `inter_spec` but breaks `cons_computable` (its witness needs to be *in `Q'X`'s own index
    type*). **The fix**: stop indexing `D'x`'s neighbourhoods by lists folded through `Uinter`, and
    instead index them by a **binary term algebra** ‚Äî `leafCode j ‚Ü¶ r j`, `nodeCode t1 t2 ‚Ü¶ Uinter
    (val t1) (val t2)`, `masterCode ‚Ü¶ masterIdx`, `Nat.pair`-encoded (`TermAlgebra` section) ‚Äî so that
    combining two already-built codes is *literally* the `node` constructor, staying inside the index
    type by construction (no search needed to name the combined index). Evaluating a code needs
    **course-of-values recursion** (a node's two children are only known `‚â§` the parent via
    `Nat.unpair`, not decreasing by a fixed amount); this reuses the *already-built, generic*
    `fuelTable`/`fuelTable_eq_of_recursion`/`primrec_fuelTable` machinery from `Recursive.lean` (built
    there for `decodeFuelOkChar`/`autStateCardFuelChar`), giving a fuel-free evaluator `TreeVal` with
    unfolding lemmas at each constructor (`TreeVal_leaf`/`_node`/`_master`, plus tag-generic forms
    `TreeVal_of_tag0`/`_tag1`/`_tag_ge2` for the `mem_X` induction) and primitive recursiveness
    (`primrec_TreeVal`). `Q2X r c := UX (TreeVal r c)` re-proves `mem_X` (strong induction on `c`,
    tag-dispatch, reusing `UX_Uinter_dichotomy`/`nbhdGen_inter`/`interFrom_append_eq` exactly as
    `toSubsystemSys_mem_foldl_Uinter` did) and `surj` (bridged to the already-proven list-based
    `Q'x_surj` via `listToTreeAux`, a fold-shaped embedding `List ‚Ñï ‚Üí ‚Ñï` with `TreeVal r
    (listToTreeAux acc l) = l.foldl (fun a j => Uinter a (r j)) (TreeVal r acc)`, identified with
    `idxchain`'s own fold via `List.foldl_map` ‚Äî no fresh combinatorial work). **The crux**:
    `Q2inter n m := nodeCode n m` now satisfies `inter_spec` *and* `cons_computable` simultaneously ‚Äî
    `Uinter_spec` applies exactly when the consistency hypothesis holds, so `UX_Uinter_dichotomy`'s
    fallback branch provably never fires on this witness, for *either* field. `interEq_computable`
    is a pure reindexing of `U_interEq_computable` along the primitive-recursive `TreeVal r` (mirroring
    `ComputablePresentation.reindexInvolutive`'s pattern, minus the involution ‚Äî `.comp` only composes
    forward). All choice-free modulo the same pre-existing `UX`/`Definition87.lean` Mathlib-`‚Ñö`-order
    `Classical.choice` artifact (confirmed by auditing `Q2x_mem_X`/`Q2x_surj`/`Q2_interEq_computable`/
    `Q2_cons_computable`/`Q2inter_spec` directly ‚Äî nothing new).
  * **6f (capstone `IsEffectivelyGiven`) ‚úÖ.** `Q'xPresentation` assembles `Q2X`/`Q2x_mem_X`/`Q2x_surj`/
    `Q2_interEq_computable`/`Q2_cons_computable`/`Q2inter`/`Q2inter_spec`/`masterCode`/
    `Q2X_masterIdx_spec` into a genuine `ComputablePresentation (toSubsystemSys UP x)`.
    `subsystemU_effectivelyGiven_of_isComputableElement`: if `x` is a computable element of `SubD UP`,
    then `D'x := toSubsystemSys UP x` is effectively given ‚Äî completing, for `D = ùí∞`, the "computable
    elements correspond to effectively presented domains" half of Exercise 8.15, relative to `UP`'s own
    enumeration.
  * **6g**: record explicitly (in-file and here) that the fully general converse ‚Äî *every*
    abstract presentation of `D'x` is effectively isomorphic to the `UP`-relative one 6e/6f built ‚Äî is
    **deliberately not attempted**: it is a deeper "uniqueness of computable numberings" fact
    (Rogers-style), is genuinely what Scott's "(up to effective isomorphism)" parenthetical is doing
    work for, and is out of scope here.

#### Exercise 8.16
* **Mathematical Target:** for finitary projections `a,b:E‚ÜíE`, `a ‚äë b ‚Üî D_a ‚óÅ D_b` where `D_a = {X ‚àà E | X ‚äë aX}`; if `E` is effectively given and `a:E‚ÜíE` is computable, then `D_a` is effectively given
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise816.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** Both halves were already (nearly) proved by existing machinery, so this is a thin assembly. `D_a` is exactly Theorem 8.5's `fixedNbhd a`. Part 1 (`isFinitaryProjection_le_iff_fixedNbhd_subsystem`) restricts Theorem 8.6(a)'s order-isomorphism `finitaryProjectionSubsystemEquiv : {f | sub f = f} ‚âÉo {D | D ‚óÅ E}` (where `‚â§` on the right is literally `‚óÅ`, Prop 6.11) from `sub`-fixed points to finitary projections via `sub_eq_self_iff_isFinitaryProjection`, assembled from `OrderIso.monotone`/`.symm.monotone`/`.symm_apply_apply` rather than the generated `map_rel_iff` (to sidestep guessing Mathlib's implicit-argument names). Part 2 is *already* Theorem 8.8(c)'s `fixedNbhd_isEffectivelyGiven` (`Theorem88m.lean`) in full generality ‚Äî `IsComputableMap P P a` for any `ComputablePresentation P` of any `E` already packages "`E` effectively given via `P`, `a` computable relative to `P`" ‚Äî so Part 2 needed no new proof, only a restatement under the exercise's name (`exercise_8_16`). Choice-free (`‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`).

#### Exercise 8.17
* **Mathematical Target:** find explicit projection pairs for `ùí∞+ùí∞`, `ùí∞√óùí∞`, `ùí∞‚Üíùí∞` needed for 8.9; are any of these isomorphic to `ùí∞`?; find a universal domain `V ‚âÝ ùí∞`
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise817.lean`

This needed one new general-purpose tool not yet in the codebase: **`‚ä¥` is transitive** (`trianglelefteq_trans`), built via a small local heterogeneous `ProjPair` bundle (`ProjPair.ofSubsystem` from Prop 6.12, `ProjPair.ofIso` from Theorem 2.7's `ofIso` ‚Äî built via `le_iff_toElementMap_le` rather than the classical `ext_of_toElementMap`, to stay choice-free ‚Äî and `ProjPair.comp`), composed and fed to Lemma 6.15's `trianglelefteq_of_projectionPair`. **Part 2** (is `ùí∞+ùí∞`/`ùí∞√óùí∞`/`ùí∞‚Üíùí∞` ‚âÖ `ùí∞`?) is **deliberately deferred**, documented rather than guessed at: only the one-directional embeddings `‚ä¥ ùí∞` come for free; genuine isomorphism would need a converse embedding plus a back-and-forth argument of the same scale as Exercise 8.12's 7-part development, and Scott's own parenthetical ("the author does not know a really good construction for `ùí∞‚Üíùí∞`") flags that even he did not resolve the `‚Üí` case. `lake build` (whole project) green, zero `sorry`. Axiom audit: `trianglelefteq_trans`/`trianglelefteq_of_isomorphic_left`/`isUniversal_of_isomorphic` fully choice-free (`‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`); the `U`/`V`-mentioning corollaries (`U_isUniversal`, `V_isUniversal`, the three `‚ä¥ ùí∞` bonuses) inherit `Classical.choice` only from `U`'s own pre-existing `Rat`-order-instance provenance, same footprint as every other `U`-mentioning headline theorem.

#### Exercise 8.19
* **Mathematical Target:** consequences of two known facts
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise819.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** Reading "we know `T`" as "`T ‚ä¥ E`" (the natural companion to `E‚ÜíE ‚ä¥ E`), the answer is **yes**, both `E+E ‚ä¥ E` and `E√óE ‚ä¥ E` follow. **Products:** `T ‚ä¥ E` gives `E√óE ‚ä¥ (T‚ÜíE)` via pairing-up-as-a-`T`-indexed-function (`pairToFun`/`funToPair`, using Exercise 3.26's `cond`), and `T ‚ä¥ E` gives `(T‚ÜíE) ‚ä¥ (E‚ÜíE)` via `expMap`'s new contravariant monotonicity lemma `expMap_mono_left` (`funSpace_dom_trianglelefteq`); chaining with `E‚ÜíE ‚ä¥ E` and `‚ä¥`'s transitivity (Exercise 8.17) gives `E√óE ‚ä¥ E` (`prod_trianglelefteq_of`). **Sums:** `T ‚ä¥ E` gives `E+E ‚ä¥ T√ó(E√óE)` (tag-and-split via `whichMap`/`outMap‚ÇÄ`/`outMap‚ÇÅ`, inverse `condSum`; two new "cross" round-trips `outMap‚ÇÅ_comp_inMap‚ÇÄ`/`outMap‚ÇÄ_comp_inMap‚ÇÅ` companion Exercise 3.18's own-side round-trips) and `T√ó(E√óE) ‚ä¥ E√ó(E√óE)` (new covariant-in-both-arguments functoriality lemmas `prod_left_trianglelefteq`/`prod_right_trianglelefteq`, the latter via `prod`'s commutativity isomorphism, Exercise 3.15); composing with `E√óE ‚ä¥ E` (applied twice, to peel off each product layer) and transitivity gives `E+E ‚ä¥ E` (`sum_trianglelefteq_of`). One genuine subtlety: `TD.bot` (`Exercise326.TD`, i.e. `Example12.neighborhoodSystem`) and `Example23.botElt` are the *same* element but not `rfl`-unifiable through the `abbrev` chain (dot-notation field projection doesn't delta-reduce transparently); proved instead by antisymmetry (`TD_bot_eq_botElt`). `lake build` (whole project) green, zero `sorry`, zero new warnings. Axiom audit: `exercise_8_19 ‚äÜ {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}`, the same pre-existing footprint as every other `T`/`cond`-mentioning theorem (from `ext_of_toElementMap` inside `expMap`'s defining lemmas and from `T`'s concrete presentation, Example 1.2), not something new.

#### Exercise 8.20
* **Mathematical Target:** `D ‚ä¥ D+D`; what about other constructs?
* **Lean File:** `Scott1980/Neighborhood/Exercise820.lean`
* **Proof Notes:** `D ‚ä¥ D√óD` and `D ‚ä¥ (D‚ÜíD)` both hold **unconditionally, for every domain `D`** (no hypotheses needed, unlike Exercise 8.19's `E√óE ‚ä¥ E`), by the simplest possible combinator recipes, formalized slightly generally over two domains `A`,`B`: **product** ‚Äî embed `a ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®a,‚ä•‚ü©`/`b ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®‚ä•,b‚ü©` (`paired (idMap _) (constMap _ bot)`), retract with `proj‚ÇÄ`/`proj‚ÇÅ` (`trianglelefteq_prod_fst`/`trianglelefteq_prod_snd`, `Proposition 3.2(i)`'s `pair_le_pair_iff` reduces the inequality half to `‚ä• ‚â§ z.snd`); **function space** ‚Äî embed `b ‚Ü¶ (Œª_. b)` (`curry (proj‚ÇÄ B A)`, `constFunMap`), retract by evaluating at `‚ä•` (`evalMap` composed with a constant-at-`‚ä•` pairing, `evalBotMap`), with the inequality half following from **monotonicity of approximable maps** (`toElementMap_mono`, Prop 2.2(iii)) applied to `‚ä• ‚â§ x`. Specializing `A=B=D` gives the two `‚ä¥` facts (`D_trianglelefteq_prod`/`D_trianglelefteq_funSpace`, bundled as `exercise_8_20`). `D ‚ä¥ D+D` itself is treated as background (Scott states it as already known, not part of the question) and not re-derived. **Multiplicity:** for products, the two constructions are already provably *different maps* whenever `D` has an element `‚âÝ ‚ä•` (`embedFst_ne_embedSnd_of_ne_bot`, via `fst_pair`) ‚Äî so yes, more than one in general; for `D‚ÜíD`, the "evaluate at a fixed point" half is forced to be `‚ä•` (any other fixed point `a` would need `a ‚â§ x` for *every* `x`), but automorphism-conjugates of the one construction shown give further pairs whenever `Aut(D)` is nontrivial (recorded as a discussion point, not formalized, since it depends on `D`'s own automorphism group). **Computability:** every combinator used (`‚ä•`, `paired`, `proj‚ÇÄ`/`proj‚ÇÅ`, `curry`, `evalMap`, `constMap`) has (or trivially would have) an `IsComputableMap` closure lemma elsewhere in the project (`Theorem74.lean`/`Theorem75.lean`), so both pairs are computable whenever `D` is effectively given ‚Äî recorded as a citation-backed answer rather than reformalized (assembling the precise `‚Ñï‚Üí‚Ñï` encoding parameters those lemmas expect is bookkeeping proportional to a full computable-presentation transport, disproportionate to this exercise). `lake build` (whole project) green, zero `sorry`, zero new warnings. Axiom audit: **every theorem in this file, including the two headline `‚ä¥` facts, is fully `‚äÜ {propext, Quot.sound}`** (no `Classical.choice` at all) ‚Äî even the map *equalities* were proved via `le_antisymm` on `le_iff_toElementMap_le`-unfolded goals rather than the choice-tainting `ApproximableMap.ext_of_toElementMap`, since both `‚â§`-directions are literal equalities of `toElementMap`s, not just comparisons (per the project's stated choice discipline).
